\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga500e332f5be1c1351a53c13383d311d6}\label{group__emac__api_ga500e332f5be1c1351a53c13383d311d6}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACIntStatus@{EMACIntStatus}}
\index{EMACIntStatus@{EMACIntStatus}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACIntStatus()}{EMACIntStatus()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACInt\+Status (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{bool}]{b\+Masked }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Gets the current Ethernet MAC interrupt status.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet MAC. \\
\hline
{\em b\+Masked} & is {\bfseries{true}} to return the masked interrupt status or {\bfseries{false}} to return the unmasked status.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function returns the interrupt status for the Ethernet MAC. Either the raw interrupt status or the status of interrupts that are allowed to reflect to the processor can be returned.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the current interrupt status as the logical OR of any of the following\+:
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+PHY}} indicates that the PHY interrupt has occurred. Software must read the relevant PHY interrupt status register to determine the cause.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+EARLY\+\_\+\+RECEIVE}} indicates that the DMA engine has filled the first data buffer of a packet.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+BUS\+\_\+\+ERROR}} indicates that a fatal bus error has occurred and that the DMA engine has been disabled. The cause of the error can be determined by calling \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gada95d93a0772edd5a0e439739b630cec}{EMACDMAState\+Get()}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+EARLY\+\_\+\+TRANSMIT}} indicates that a frame to be transmitted has been fully written from memory into the MAC transmit FIFO.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+WATCHDOG}} indicates that a frame with length greater than 2048 bytes (of 10240 bytes in Jumbo Frame mode) was received.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+STOPPED}} indicates that the receive process has entered the stopped state.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+BUFFER}} indicates that the host owns the next buffer in the DMA\textquotesingle{}s receive descriptor list and the DMA cannot, therefore, acquire a buffer. The receive process is suspended and can be resumed by changing the descriptor ownership and calling \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga473bdac3a4d64d1b975785811d5ca38d}{EMACRx\+DMAPoll\+Demand()}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RECEIVE}} indicates that reception of a frame has completed and all requested status has been written to the appropriate DMA receive descriptor.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+UNDERFLOW}} indicates that the transmitter experienced an underflow during transmission. The transmit process is suspended.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+OVERFLOW}} indicates that an overflow was experienced during reception.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+JABBER}} indicates that the transmit jabber timer expired. This condition occurs when the frame size exceeds 2048 bytes (or 10240 bytes in Jumbo Frame mode) and causes the transmit process to abort and enter the Stopped state.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+BUFFER}} indicates that the host owns the next buffer in the DMA\textquotesingle{}s transmit descriptor list and that the DMA cannot, therefore, acquire a buffer. Transmission is suspended and can be resumed by changing the descriptor ownership and calling \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga3cafbfbc7de989bec229f26765094dd5}{EMACTx\+DMAPoll\+Demand()}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+STOPPED}} indicates that the transmit process has stopped.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TRANSMIT}} indicates that transmission of a frame has completed and that all requested status has been updated in the descriptor.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+NORMAL\+\_\+\+INT}} is a summary interrupt comprising the logical OR of the masked state of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TRANSMIT}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RECEIVE}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+BUFFER}} and {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+EARLY\+\_\+\+RECEIVE}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+ABNORMAL\+\_\+\+INT}} is a summary interrupt comprising the logical OR of the masked state of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+STOPPED}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+JABBER}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+OVERFLOW}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+UNDERFLOW}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+NO\+\_\+\+BUFFER}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+STOPPED}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+WATCHDOG}}, {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+EARLY\+\_\+\+TRANSMIT}} and {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+BUS\+\_\+\+ERROR}}. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga9d5cb58f12b3cb787e6d796f47bb6f30}\label{group__emac__api_ga9d5cb58f12b3cb787e6d796f47bb6f30}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACIntUnregister@{EMACIntUnregister}}
\index{EMACIntUnregister@{EMACIntUnregister}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACIntUnregister()}{EMACIntUnregister()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACInt\+Unregister (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Unregisters an interrupt handler for an Ethernet interrupt.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function unregisters the interrupt handler. This function disables the global interrupt in the interrupt controller so that the interrupt handler is no longer called.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga06aa7ee17a6c9cd21ab327167a74158e}\label{group__emac__api_ga06aa7ee17a6c9cd21ab327167a74158e}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACNumAddrGet@{EMACNumAddrGet}}
\index{EMACNumAddrGet@{EMACNumAddrGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACNumAddrGet()}{EMACNumAddrGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACNum\+Addr\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the number of MAC addresses supported by the Ethernet controller.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function may be used to determine the number of MAC addresses that the given controller supports. MAC address slots may be used when performing perfect (rather than hash table) filtering of packets.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the number of supported MAC addresses. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga6f369bdbe2e8ea108ef1398242030198}\label{group__emac__api_ga6f369bdbe2e8ea108ef1398242030198}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACPHYConfigSet@{EMACPHYConfigSet}}
\index{EMACPHYConfigSet@{EMACPHYConfigSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACPHYConfigSet()}{EMACPHYConfigSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACPHYConfig\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Config }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Selects the Ethernet PHY in use.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller. \\
\hline
{\em ui32\+Config} & selects the PHY in use and, when using the internal PHY, allows various various PHY parameters to be configured.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function must be called prior to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga453520ef2871a0eaef9068288c5cf9a1}{EMACInit()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gac5f841841defc3ca16794ca95508dcea}{EMACConfig\+Set()}} to select the Ethernet PHY to be used. If the internal PHY is selected, the function also allows configuration of various PHY parameters. Note that the Ethernet MAC is reset during this function call because parameters used by this function are latched by the hardware only on a MAC reset. The call sequence to select and configure the PHY, therefore, must be as follows\+:

\begin{DoxyVerb}//!     // Enable and reset the MAC.
//!     SysCtlPeripheralEnable(SYSCTL_PERIPH_EMAC0);
//!     SysCtlPeripheralReset(SYSCTL_PERIPH_EMAC0);
//!     if(<using internal PHY>)
//!     {
//!         // Enable and reset the internal PHY.
//!         SysCtlPeripheralEnable(SYSCTL_PERIPH_EPHY0);
//!         SysCtlPeripheralReset(SYSCTL_PERIPH_EPHY0);
//!     }
//!
//!     // Ensure the MAC is completed its reset.
//!     while(!MAP_SysCtlPeripheralReady(SYSCTL_PERIPH_EMAC0))
//!     {
//!     }
//!
//!     // Set the PHY type and configuration options.
//!     EMACPHYConfigSet(EMAC0_BASE, <config>);
//!
//!     // Initialize and configure the MAC.
//!     EMACInit(EMAC0_BASE, <system clock rate>, <bus config>,
//!              <Rx burst size>, <Tx burst size>, <desc skip>);
//!     EMACConfigSet(EMAC0_BASE, <parameters>);
//! \end{DoxyVerb}
 \begin{DoxyVerb}The \e ui32Config parameter must specify one of the following values:

- \b EMAC_PHY_TYPE_INTERNAL selects the internal Ethernet PHY.
- \b EMAC_PHY_TYPE_EXTERNAL_MII selects an external PHY connected via the
MII interface.
- \b EMAC_PHY_TYPE_EXTERNAL_RMII selects an external PHY connected via the
RMII interface.

If \b EMAC_PHY_TYPE_INTERNAL is selected, the following flags may be ORed
into \e ui32Config to control various PHY features and modes.  These flags 
are ignored if an external PHY is selected.

- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_NIB_TXERR_DET_DIS disables odd nibble transmit error
detection (sets the default value of PHY register MR10, bit 1).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_RX_ER_DURING_IDLE enables receive error detection during
idle  (sets the default value of PHY register MR10, bit 2).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_ISOLATE_MII_LLOSS ties the MII outputs low if no link is
established in 100B-T and full duplex modes (sets the default value of PHY
register MR10, bit 3).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_LINK_LOSS_RECOVERY enables link loss recovery (sets the
default value of PHY register MR9, bit 7).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_TDRRUN enables execution of the TDR procedure after a link
down event (sets the default value of PHY register MR9, bit 8).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_LD_ON_RX_ERR_COUNT enables link down if the receiver
error count reaches 32 within a 10-us interval (sets the default value of
PHY register MR11 bit 3).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_LD_ON_MTL3_ERR_COUNT enables link down if the MTL3 error
count reaches 20 in a 10 us-interval (sets the default value of PHY register
MR11 bit 2).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_LD_ON_LOW_SNR enables link down if the low SNR threshold
is crossed 20 times in a 10 us-interval (sets the default value of PHY
register MR11 bit 1).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_LD_ON_SIGNAL_ENERGY enables link down if energy detector
indicates Energy Loss (sets the default value of PHY register MR11 bit 0).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_POLARITY_SWAP inverts the polarity on both TPTD and TPRD
pairs (sets the default value of PHY register MR11 bit 5).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_MDI_SWAP swaps the MDI pairs putting receive on the TPTD
pair and transmit on TPRD (sets the default value of PHY register MR11 bit
6).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_ROBUST_MDIX enables robust auto MDI-X resolution (sets the
default value of PHY register MR9 bit 5).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_MDIX enables fast auto-MDI/MDIX resolution (sets the
default value of PHY register MR9 bit 6).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_MDIX_EN enables auto-MDI/MDIX crossover (sets the
default value of PHY register MR9 bit 14).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_RXDV_DETECT enables fast RXDV detection (set the
default value of PHY register MR9 bit 1).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_L_UP_DETECT enables fast link-up time during parallel
detection (sets the default value of PHY register MR10 bit 6)
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_EXT_FULL_DUPLEX forces full-duplex while working with a
link partner in forced 100B-TX (sets the default value of PHY register
MR10 bit 5).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_AN_80_50_35 enables fast auto-negotiation using
break link, link fail inhibit and wait timers set to 80, 50 and 35
respectively (sets the default value of PHY register MR9 bits [4:2] to
3b100).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_AN_120_75_50 enables fast auto-negotiation using
break link, link fail inhibit and wait timers set to 120, 75 and 50
respectively (sets the default value of PHY register MR9 bits [4:2] to
3b101).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_FAST_AN_140_150_100 enables fast auto-negotiation using
break link, link fail inhibit and wait timers set to 140, 150 and 100
respectively (sets the default value of PHY register MR9 bits [4:2] to
3b110).
- \b EMAC_PHY_FORCE_10B_T_HALF_DUPLEX disables auto-negotiation and forces
operation in 10Base-T, half duplex mode (sets the default value of PHY
register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b000).
- \b EMAC_PHY_FORCE_10B_T_FULL_DUPLEX disables auto-negotiation and forces
operation in 10Base-T, full duplex mode (sets the default value of PHY
register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b001).
- \b EMAC_PHY_FORCE_100B_T_HALF_DUPLEX disables auto-negotiation and forces
operation in 100Base-T, half duplex mode (sets the default value of PHY
register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b010).
- \b EMAC_PHY_FORCE_100B_T_FULL_DUPLEX disables auto-negotiation and forces
operation in 100Base-T, full duplex mode (sets the default value of PHY
register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b011).
- \b EMAC_PHY_AN_10B_T_HALF_DUPLEX enables auto-negotiation and advertises
10Base-T, half duplex mode (sets the default value of PHY register MR9 bits
[13:11] to 3b100).
- \b EMAC_PHY_AN_10B_T_FULL_DUPLEX enables auto-negotiation and advertises
10Base-T half or full duplex modes (sets the default value of PHY register
MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b101).
- \b EMAC_PHY_AN_100B_T_HALF_DUPLEX enables auto-negotiation and advertises
10Base-T half or full duplex, and 100Base-T half duplex modes (sets the
default value of PHY register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b110).
- \b EMAC_PHY_AN_100B_T_FULL_DUPLEX enables auto-negotiation and advertises
10Base-T half or full duplex, and 100Base-T half or full duplex modes (sets
the default value of PHY register MR9 bits [13:11] to 3b111).
- \b EMAC_PHY_INT_HOLD prevents the PHY from transmitting energy on the
line.

As a side effect of this function, the Ethernet MAC is reset so any
previous MAC configuration is lost.

\return None. 
\end{DoxyVerb}
 \mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga6b3428f8d47bf7d0c802283bda1909e2}\label{group__emac__api_ga6b3428f8d47bf7d0c802283bda1909e2}}

\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACPowerManagementControlGet@{EMACPowerManagementControlGet}}
\index{EMACPowerManagementControlGet@{EMACPowerManagementControlGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACPowerManagementControlGet()}{EMACPowerManagementControlGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACPower\+Management\+Control\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Queries the current Ethernet MAC remote wake-\/up configuration.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function allows the MAC\textquotesingle{}s remote wake-\/up settings to be queried. These settings determine which types of frame should trigger a remote wake-\/up event

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a logical OR of the following flags\+:
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+GLOBAL\+\_\+\+UNICAST\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} indicates that the MAC wakes up when any unicast frame matching the MAC destination address filter is received.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+WAKEUP\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} indicates that the MAC wakes up when any received frame matches the remote wake-\/up filter configured via a call to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga011f5a2a72640eea9a785fdc108f2784}{EMACRemote\+Wake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter\+Set()}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+MAGIC\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} indicates that the MAC wakes up when a standard Wake-\/on-\/\+LAN \char`\"{}magic packet\char`\"{} is received. The magic packet contains 6 bytes of 0x\+FF followed immediately by 16 repetitions of the destination MAC address.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+POWER\+\_\+\+DOWN}} indicates that the MAC is currently in power-\/down mode and is waiting for an incoming frame matching the remote wake-\/up frames as described by other returned flags and via the remote wake-\/up filter. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga447fd24e3ea71e1cca2e092b93aa5e90}\label{group__emac__api_ga447fd24e3ea71e1cca2e092b93aa5e90}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACPowerManagementControlSet@{EMACPowerManagementControlSet}}
\index{EMACPowerManagementControlSet@{EMACPowerManagementControlSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACPowerManagementControlSet()}{EMACPowerManagementControlSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACPower\+Management\+Control\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Flags }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the Ethernet MAC remote wake-\/up configuration.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em ui32\+Flags} & defines which types of frame should trigger a remote wake-\/up and allows the MAC to be put into power-\/down mode.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function allows the MAC\textquotesingle{}s remote wake-\/up features to be configured, determining which types of frame should trigger a wake-\/up event and allowing an application to place the MAC in power-\/down mode. In this mode, the MAC ignores all received frames until one matching a configured remote wake-\/up frame is received, at which point the MAC automatically exits power-\/down mode and continues to receive frames.

The {\itshape ui32\+Flags} parameter is a logical OR of the following flags\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+GLOBAL\+\_\+\+UNICAST\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} instructs the MAC to wake up when any unicast frame matching the MAC destination address filter is received.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+WAKEUP\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} instructs the MAC to wake up when any received frame matches the remote wake-\/up filter configured via a call to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga011f5a2a72640eea9a785fdc108f2784}{EMACRemote\+Wake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter\+Set()}}.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+MAGIC\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} instructs the MAC to wake up when a standard Wake-\/on-\/\+LAN \char`\"{}magic packet\char`\"{} is received. The magic packet contains 6 bytes of 0x\+FF followed immediately by 16 repetitions of the destination MAC address.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+POWER\+\_\+\+DOWN}} instructs the MAC to enter power-\/down mode and wait for an incoming frame matching the remote wake-\/up frames as described by other flags and via the remote wake-\/up filter. This flag should only set set if at least one other flag is specified to configure a wake-\/up frame type.
\end{DoxyItemize}

When the MAC is in power-\/down mode, software may exit the mode by calling this function with the {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+POWER\+\_\+\+DOWN}} flag absent from {\itshape ui32\+Flags}. If a configured wake-\/up frame is received while in power-\/down mode, the {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+INT\+\_\+\+POWER\+\_\+\+MGMNT}} interrupt is signaled and may be cleared by reading the status using \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gac8d1ba09e288c496262591692be94fe2}{EMACPower\+Management\+Status\+Get()}}.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
While it is possible to gate the clock to the MAC while it is in power-\/down mode, doing so prevents the reading of the registers required to determine the interrupt status and also prevents power-\/down mode from exiting via another call to this function.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_gac8d1ba09e288c496262591692be94fe2}\label{group__emac__api_gac8d1ba09e288c496262591692be94fe2}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACPowerManagementStatusGet@{EMACPowerManagementStatusGet}}
\index{EMACPowerManagementStatusGet@{EMACPowerManagementStatusGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACPowerManagementStatusGet()}{EMACPowerManagementStatusGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACPower\+Management\+Status\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Queries the current Ethernet MAC remote wake-\/up status.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function returns information on the remote wake-\/up state of the Ethernet MAC. If the MAC has been woken up since the last call, the returned value indicates the type of received frame that caused the MAC to exit power-\/down state.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a logical OR of the following flags\+:
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+POWER\+\_\+\+DOWN}} indicates that the MAC is currently in power-\/down mode.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+WAKEUP\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+RECEIVED}} indicates that the MAC exited power-\/down mode due to a remote wake-\/up frame being received. This function call clears this flag.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+PMT\+\_\+\+MAGIC\+\_\+\+PACKET\+\_\+\+RECEIVED}} indicates that the MAC exited power-\/down mode due to a wake-\/on-\/\+LAN magic packet being received. This function call clears this flag. 
\end{DoxyItemize}\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga50ad8fc16e031c90ced4f023b0692cbc}\label{group__emac__api_ga50ad8fc16e031c90ced4f023b0692cbc}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet@{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet}}
\index{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet@{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet()}{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACRemote\+Wake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_wake_up_frame_filter}{t\+EMACWake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter}} $\ast$}]{p\+Filter }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the current remote wake-\/up frame filter configuration.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em p\+Filter} & points to the structure that is written with the current remote wake-\/up frame filter information.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function may be used to read the current wake-\/up frame filter settings. The data returned by the function describes wake-\/up frames in terms of a CRC calculated on up to 31 payload bytes in the frame. The actual bytes used in the CRC calculation are defined by means of a bit mask where a {\ttfamily 1\textquotesingle{}\textquotesingle{} indicates that a byte in the frame should contribute to the CRC calculation and a}0\textquotesingle{}\textquotesingle{} indicates that the byte should be skipped, and an offset from the start of the frame to the payload byte that represents the first byte in the 31-\/byte CRC-\/checked sequence.

The {\itshape p\+Filter} parameter points to storage that is written with a structure containing the information defining the frame filters. This structure contains the following fields, each of which is replicated 4 times, once for each possible wake-\/up frame\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}} defines whether a given byte in the chosen 31-\/byte sequence within the frame should contribute to the CRC calculation or not. A 1 indicates that the byte should contribute to the calculation, a 0 causes the byte to be skipped.
\item {\bfseries{pui8\+Command}} contains flags defining whether this filter is enabled and, if so, whether it refers to unicast or multicast packets. Valid values are one of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+MULTICAST}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+UNICAST}} ORed with one of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+DISABLE}}.
\item {\bfseries{pui8\+Offset}} defines the zero-\/based index of the byte within the frame at which CRC checking defined by {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}} begins. Alternatively, this value can be thought of as the number of bytes in the frame that the MAC skips before accumulating the CRC based on the pattern in {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}}.
\item {\bfseries{pui16\+CRC}} provides the value of the calculated CRC for a valid remote wake-\/up frame. If the incoming frame is processed according to the filter values provided and the final CRC calculation equals this value, the frame is considered to be a valid remote wake-\/up frame.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Note that this filter uses CRC16 rather than CRC32 as used in frame checksums.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga011f5a2a72640eea9a785fdc108f2784}\label{group__emac__api_ga011f5a2a72640eea9a785fdc108f2784}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet@{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet}}
\index{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet@{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet()}{EMACRemoteWakeUpFrameFilterSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACRemote\+Wake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_wake_up_frame_filter}{t\+EMACWake\+Up\+Frame\+Filter}} $\ast$}]{p\+Filter }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets values defining up to four frames used to trigger a remote wake-\/up.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em p\+Filter} & points to the structure containing remote wake-\/up frame filter information.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function may be used to define up to four different frames that are considered by the Ethernet MAC to be remote wake-\/up signals. The data passed to the function describes a wake-\/up frame in terms of a CRC calculated on up to 31 payload bytes in the frame. The actual bytes used in the CRC calculation are defined by means of a bit mask where a \`{}`1'\textquotesingle{} indicates that a byte in the frame should contribute to the CRC calculation and a \`{}`0'\textquotesingle{} indicates that the byte should be skipped, as well as an offset from the start of the frame to the payload byte that represents the first byte in the 31-\/byte CRC-\/checked sequence.

The {\itshape p\+Filter} parameter points to a structure containing the information necessary to set up the filters. This structure contains the following fields, each of which is replicated 4 times, once for each possible wake-\/up frame\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}} defines whether a given byte in the chosen 31-\/byte sequence within the frame should contribute to the CRC calculation or not. A 1 indicates that the byte should contribute to the calculation, a 0 causes the byte to be skipped.
\item {\bfseries{pui8\+Command}} contains flags defining whether this filter is enabled and, if so, whether it refers to unicast or multicast packets. Valid values are one of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+MULTICAST}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+UNICAST}} ORed with one of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+RWU\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+DISABLE}}.
\item {\bfseries{pui8\+Offset}} defines the zero-\/based index of the byte within the frame at which CRC checking defined by {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}} begins. Alternatively, this value can be thought of as the number of bytes in the frame that the MAC skips before accumulating the CRC based on the pattern ~\newline
 in {\bfseries{pui32\+Byte\+Mask}}.
\item {\bfseries{pui16\+CRC}} provides the value of the calculated CRC for a valid remote wake-\/up frame. If the incoming frame is processed according to the filter values provided and the final CRC calculation equals this value, the frame is considered to be a valid remote wake-\/up frame.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Note that this filter uses CRC16 rather than CRC32 as used in frame checksums. The required CRC uses a direct algorithm with polynomial 0x8005, initial seed value 0x\+FFFF, no final XOR and reversed data order. CRCs for use in this function may be determined using the online calculator found at \href{http://www.zorc.breitbandkatze.de/crc.html}{\texttt{ http\+://www.\+zorc.\+breitbandkatze.\+de/crc.\+html}}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_gac6bdbf26467dc58bbe45f19ba992d027}\label{group__emac__api_gac6bdbf26467dc58bbe45f19ba992d027}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACReset@{EMACReset}}
\index{EMACReset@{EMACReset}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACReset()}{EMACReset()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACReset (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Resets the Ethernet MAC.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function performs a reset of the Ethernet MAC by resetting all logic and returning all registers to their default values. The function returns only after the hardware indicates that the reset has completed.

\begin{DoxyNote}{Note}
To ensure that the reset completes, the selected PHY clock must be enabled when this function is called. If the PHY clock is absent, this function does not return.
\end{DoxyNote}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga53c294e11c1fe14d1d4e5db323172fc3}\label{group__emac__api_ga53c294e11c1fe14d1d4e5db323172fc3}}

\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxDMACurrentBufferGet@{EMACRxDMACurrentBufferGet}}

\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxDMACurrentDescriptorGet@{EMACRxDMACurrentDescriptorGet}}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_d_m_a_descriptor}{t\+EMACDMADescriptor}} $\ast$ EMACRx\+DMACurrent\+Descriptor\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet@{EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet}}
\index{EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet@{EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet()}{EMACRxDMADescriptorListGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_d_m_a_descriptor}{t\+EMACDMADescriptor}} $\ast$ EMACRx\+DMADescriptor\+List\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns a pointer to the start of the DMA receive descriptor list.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function returns a pointer to the head of the Ethernet MAC\textquotesingle{}s receive DMA descriptor list. This value corresponds to the pointer originally set using a call to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga5e6f25424033425b90e0701ae1c69c1f}{EMACRx\+DMADescriptor\+List\+Set()}}.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns a pointer to the start of the DMA receive descriptor list. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga5e6f25424033425b90e0701ae1c69c1f}\label{group__emac__api_ga5e6f25424033425b90e0701ae1c69c1f}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet@{EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet}}
\index{EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet@{EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet()}{EMACRxDMADescriptorListSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACRx\+DMADescriptor\+List\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_d_m_a_descriptor}{t\+EMACDMADescriptor}} $\ast$}]{p\+Descriptor }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the DMA receive descriptor list pointer.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em p\+Descriptor} & points to the first DMA descriptor in the list to be passed to the receive DMA engine.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function sets the Ethernet MAC\textquotesingle{}s receive DMA descriptor list pointer. The {\itshape p\+Descriptor} pointer must point to one or more descriptor structures.

When multiple descriptors are provided, they can be either chained or unchained. Chained descriptors are indicated by setting the {\bfseries{DES0\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+CTRL\+\_\+\+CHAINED}} or {\bfseries{DES1\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+CTRL\+\_\+\+CHAINED}} bit in the relevant word of the transmit or receive descriptor. If this bit is clear, unchained descriptors are assumed.

Chained descriptors use a link pointer in each descriptor to point to the next descriptor in the chain.

Unchained descriptors are assumed to be contiguous in memory with a consistent offset between the start of one descriptor and the next. If unchained descriptors are used, the {\itshape pv\+Link} field in the descriptor becomes available to store a second buffer pointer, allowing each descriptor to point to two buffers rather than one. In this case, the {\itshape ui32\+Desc\+Skip\+Size} parameter to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_ga453520ef2871a0eaef9068288c5cf9a1}{EMACInit()}} must previously have been set to the number of words between the end of one descriptor and the start of the next. This value must be 0 in cases where a packed array of {\bfseries{\mbox{\hyperlink{structt_e_m_a_c_d_m_a_descriptor}{t\+EMACDMADescriptor}}}} structures is used. If the application wishes to add new state fields to the end of the descriptor structure, the skip size should be set to accommodate the newly sized structure.

Applications are responsible for initializing all descriptor fields appropriately before passing the descriptor list to the hardware.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga473bdac3a4d64d1b975785811d5ca38d}\label{group__emac__api_ga473bdac3a4d64d1b975785811d5ca38d}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxDMAPollDemand@{EMACRxDMAPollDemand}}
\index{EMACRxDMAPollDemand@{EMACRxDMAPollDemand}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRxDMAPollDemand()}{EMACRxDMAPollDemand()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACRx\+DMAPoll\+Demand (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Orders the MAC DMA controller to attempt to acquire the next receive descriptor.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function must be called to restart the receiver if it has been suspended due to the current receive DMA descriptor being owned by the host. Once the application reads any data from the descriptor and marks it as being owned by the MAC DMA, this function causes the hardware to attempt to acquire the descriptor before writing the next received packet into its buffer(s).

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga3cf71b1750544b3c34b37766e72232b8}\label{group__emac__api_ga3cf71b1750544b3c34b37766e72232b8}}

\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet@{EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet}}
\index{EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet@{EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet()}{EMACRxWatchdogTimerSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACRx\+Watchdog\+Timer\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint8\+\_\+t}]{ui8\+Timeout }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the receive interrupt watchdog timer period.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller. \\
\hline
{\em ui8\+Timeout} & is the desired timeout expressed as a number of 256 system clock periods.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function configures the receive interrupt watchdog timer. The {\itshape ui\+Timeout} parameter specifies the number of 256 system clock periods that elapse before the timer expires. In cases where the DMA has transferred a frame using a descriptor that has {\bfseries{DES1\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+CTRL\+\_\+\+DISABLE\+\_\+\+INT}} set, the watchdog causes a receive interrupt to be generated when it times out. The watchdog timer is reset whenever a packet is transferred to memory using a DMA descriptor that does not disable the receive interrupt.

To disable the receive interrupt watchdog function, set {\itshape ui8\+Timeout} to 0.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga859d06d5361b527f1e1407bce4ebcbbb}\label{group__emac__api_ga859d06d5361b527f1e1407bce4ebcbbb}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACStatusGet@{EMACStatusGet}}
\index{EMACStatusGet@{EMACStatusGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACStatusGet()}{EMACStatusGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACStatus\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the current Ethernet MAC status.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the Ethernet controller.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function returns information on the current status of all the main modules in the MAC transmit and receive data paths.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the current MAC status as a logical OR of any of the following flags\+:
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+NOT\+\_\+\+EMPTY}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+WRITING\+\_\+\+FIFO}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TX\+\_\+\+PAUSED}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+MAC\+\_\+\+NOT\+\_\+\+IDLE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RWC\+\_\+\+ACTIVE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RPE\+\_\+\+ACTIVE}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

The transmit frame controller status can be extracted from the returned value by ANDing with {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TFC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+MASK}} and is one of the following\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TFC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+IDLE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TFC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+WAITING}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TFC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+PAUSING}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TFC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+WRITING}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

The transmit FIFO read controller status can be extracted from the returned value by ANDing with {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TRC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+MASK}} and is one of the following\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TRC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+IDLE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TRC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+READING}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TRC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+WAITING}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+TRC\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+STATUS}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

The current receive FIFO levels can be extracted from the returned value by ANDing with {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+LEVEL\+\_\+\+MASK}} and is one of the following\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+EMPTY}} indicating that the FIFO is empty.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+BELOW}} indicating that the FIFO fill level is below the flow-\/control deactivate threshold.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+ABOVE}} indicating that the FIFO fill level is above the flow-\/control activate threshold.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+FULL}} indicating that the FIFO is full.
\end{DoxyItemize}

The current receive FIFO state can be extracted from the returned value by ANDing with {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+STATE\+\_\+\+MASK}} and is one of the following\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+IDLE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+READING}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+STATUS}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+STATUS\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FIFO\+\_\+\+FLUSHING}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_gaf58bcf48127a67c0eda8eb96319e8690}\label{group__emac__api_gaf58bcf48127a67c0eda8eb96319e8690}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACTimestampAddendSet@{EMACTimestampAddendSet}}
\index{EMACTimestampAddendSet@{EMACTimestampAddendSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACTimestampAddendSet()}{EMACTimestampAddendSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACTimestamp\+Addend\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Increment }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Adjusts the system time update rate when using the fine correction method.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em ui32\+Increment} & is the number to add to the accumulator register on each tick of the 25-\/MHz main oscillator.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function is used to control the rate of update of the system time when in fine update mode. Fine correction mode is selected if {\itshape EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+FINE} is supplied in the {\itshape ui32\+Config} parameter passed to a previous call to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}{EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set()}}. Fine update mode is typically used when synchronizing the local clock to the IEEE 1588 master clock. The subsecond counter is incremented by the number passed to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}{EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set()}} in the {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} parameter each time a 32-\/bit accumulator register generates a carry. The accumulator register is incremented by the \char`\"{}addend\char`\"{} value on each main oscillator tick, and this addend value is modified to allow fine control over the rate of change of the timestamp counter. The addend value is calculated using the ratio of the main oscillator clock rate and the desired IEEE 1588 clock rate and the {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} value is set to correspond to the desired IEEE 1588 clock rate.

As an example, using digital rollover mode and a 25-\/MHz main oscillator clock with a desired IEEE 1588 clock accuracy of 12.\+5 MHz, and having made a previous call to \mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}{EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set()}} with {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} set to the 12.\+5-\/MHz clock period of 80 ns, the initial {\itshape ui32\+Increment} value would be set to 0x80000000 to generate a carry on every second main oscillator tick. Because the system time updates each time the accumulator overflows, small changes in the {\itshape ui32\+Increment} value can be used to very finely control the system time rate.

\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
None.
\end{DoxyReturn}
\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}{EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set()}} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_ga9de9c904c32b3f8a6515019ab6e66782}\label{group__emac__api_ga9de9c904c32b3f8a6515019ab6e66782}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACTimestampConfigGet@{EMACTimestampConfigGet}}
\index{EMACTimestampConfigGet@{EMACTimestampConfigGet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACTimestampConfigGet()}{EMACTimestampConfigGet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily uint32\+\_\+t EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Get (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t $\ast$}]{pui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Returns the current IEEE 1588 timestamping configuration.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em pui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} & points to storage that is written with the current subsecond increment value for the IEEE 1588 clock.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function may be used to retreive the current MAC timestamping configuration.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}{EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set()}}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
Returns the current timestamping configuration as a logical OR of the following flags\+:
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PTP\+\_\+\+VERSION\+\_\+2}} indicates that the MAC is processing PTP version 2 messages. If this flag is absent, PTP version 1 messages are expected.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DIGITAL\+\_\+\+ROLLOVER}} causes the clock\textquotesingle{}s subsecond value to roll over at 0x3\+BA9\+C9\+FF (999999999 decimal). In this mode, it can be considered as a nanosecond counter with each digit representing 1 ns. If this flag is absent, the subsecond value rolls over at 0x7\+FFFFFFF, effectively counting increments of 0.\+465 ns.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+MAC\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} indicates that incoming PTP messages are filtered using any of the configured MAC addresses. Messages with a destination address programmed into the MAC address filter are passed, others are discarded. If this flag is absent, the MAC address is ignored.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+FINE}} implements the fine update method that causes the IEEE 1588 clock to advance by the the value returned in the {\itshape $\ast$pui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} parameter each time a carry is generated from the addend accumulator register. If this flag is absent, the coarse update method is in use and the clock is advanced by the {\itshape $\ast$pui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} value on each system clock tick.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+ONLY}} indicates that timestamps are only generated for SYNC messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DELAYREQ\+\_\+\+ONLY}} indicates that timestamps are only generated for Delay\+\_\+\+Req messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+ALL}} indicates that timestamps are generated for all IEEE 1588 messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} timestamps only SYNC, Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DREQ\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} indicates that timestamps are only generated for Delay\+\_\+\+Req, Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+DELAYREQ}} indicates that timestamps are only generated for Delay\+\_\+\+Req messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} indicates that timestamps are only generated for Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+IPV4\+\_\+\+UDP}} indicates that PTP packets encapsulated in UDP over IPv4 packets are being processed. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+IPV6\+\_\+\+UDP}} indicates that PTP packets encapsulated in UDP over IPv6 packets are being processed. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+ETHERNET}} indicates that PTP packets encapsulated directly in Ethernet frames are being processd. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+ALL\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FRAMES}} indicates that timestamping is enabled for all frames received by the MAC, regardless of type.
\end{DoxyItemize}

If {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+ALL\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FRAMES}} and none of the options specifying subsets of PTP packets to timestamp are set, the MAC is configured to timestamp SYNC, Follow\+\_\+\+Up, Delay\+\_\+\+Req and Delay\+\_\+\+Resp messages only. \mbox{\Hypertarget{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}\label{group__emac__api_gaa1145b330c9da2d665730a51739a27d2}} 
\index{Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}!EMACTimestampConfigSet@{EMACTimestampConfigSet}}
\index{EMACTimestampConfigSet@{EMACTimestampConfigSet}!Emac\_api@{Emac\_api}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{EMACTimestampConfigSet()}{EMACTimestampConfigSet()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily void EMACTimestamp\+Config\+Set (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Base,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Config,  }\item[{uint32\+\_\+t}]{ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Configures the Ethernet MAC\textquotesingle{}s IEEE 1588 timestamping options.


\begin{DoxyParams}{Parameters}
{\em ui32\+Base} & is the base address of the controller. \\
\hline
{\em ui32\+Config} & contains flags selecting particular configuration options. \\
\hline
{\em ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} & is the number that the IEEE 1588 subsecond clock should increment on each tick.\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
This function is used to configure the operation of the Ethernet MAC\textquotesingle{}s internal timestamping clock. This clock is used to timestamp incoming and outgoing packets and as an accurate system time reference when IEEE 1588 Precision Time Protocol is in use.

The {\itshape ui32\+Config} parameter contains a collection of flags selecting the desired options. Valid flags are\+:

One of the following to determine whether IEEE 1588 version 1 or version 2 packet format is to be processed\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PTP\+\_\+\+VERSION\+\_\+2}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PTP\+\_\+\+VERSION\+\_\+1}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

One of the following to determine how the IEEE 1588 clock\textquotesingle{}s subsecond value should be interpreted and handled\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DIGITAL\+\_\+\+ROLLOVER}} causes the clock\textquotesingle{}s subsecond value to roll over at 0x3\+BA9\+C9\+FF (999999999 decimal). In this mode, it can be considered as a nanosecond counter with each digit representing 1 ns.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+BINARY\+\_\+\+ROLLOVER}} causes the clock\textquotesingle{}s subsecond value to roll over at 0x7\+FFFFFFF. In this mode, the subsecond value counts 0.\+465 ns periods.
\end{DoxyItemize}

One of the following to enable or disable MAC address filtering. When enabled, PTP frames are filtered unless the destination MAC address matches any of the currently programmed MAC addresses.


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+MAC\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+ENABLE}} 
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+MAC\+\_\+\+FILTER\+\_\+\+DISABLE}} 
\end{DoxyItemize}

One of the following to determine how the clock is updated\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+COARSE}} causes the IEEE 1588 clock to advance by the value supplied in the {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} parameter on each main oscillator clock cycle.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+FINE}} selects the fine update method which causes the IEEE 1588 clock to advance by the the value supplied in the {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} parameter each time a carry is generated from the addend accumulator register.
\end{DoxyItemize}

One of the following to determine which IEEE 1588 messages are timestamped\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+FOLLOW\+\_\+\+DREQ\+\_\+\+DRESP}} timestamps SYNC, Follow\+\_\+\+Up, Delay\+\_\+\+Req and Delay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+ONLY}} timestamps only SYNC messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DELAYREQ\+\_\+\+ONLY}} timestamps only Delay\+\_\+\+Req messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+ALL}} timestamps all IEEE 1588 messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} timestamps only SYNC, Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DREQ\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} timestamps only Delay\+\_\+\+Req, Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+SYNC\+\_\+\+DELAYREQ}} timestamps only Delay\+\_\+\+Req messages.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PDREQ\+\_\+\+PDRESP}} timestamps only Pdelay\+\_\+\+Req and Pdelay\+\_\+\+Resp messages.
\end{DoxyItemize}

Optional, additional flags are\+:


\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+IPV4\+\_\+\+UDP}} processes PTP packets encapsulated in UDP over IPv4 packets. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+IPV6\+\_\+\+UDP}} processes PTP packets encapsulated in UDP over IPv6 packets. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+PROCESS\+\_\+\+ETHERNET}} processes PTP packets encapsulated directly in Ethernet frames. If absent, the MAC ignores these frames.
\item {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+ALL\+\_\+\+RX\+\_\+\+FRAMES}} enables timestamping for all frames received by the MAC, regardless of type.
\end{DoxyItemize}

The {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} controls the rate at which the timestamp clock\textquotesingle{}s subsecond count increments. Its meaning depends on which of {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+DIGITAL\+\_\+\+ROLLOVER}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+BINARY\+\_\+\+ROLLOVER}} and {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+FINE}} or {\bfseries{EMAC\+\_\+\+TS\+\_\+\+UPDATE\+\_\+\+COARSE}} were included in {\itshape ui32\+Config}.

The timestamp second counter is incremented each time the subsecond counter rolls over. In digital rollover mode, the subsecond counter acts as a simple 31-\/bit counter, rolling over to 0 after reaching 0x7\+FFFFFFF. In this case, each lsb of the subsecond counter represents 0.\+465 ns (assuming the definition of 1 second resolution for the seconds counter). When binary rollover mode is selected, the subsecond counter acts as a nanosecond counter and rolls over to 0 after reaching 999,999,999 making each lsb represent 1 nanosecond.

In coarse update mode, the timestamp subsecond counter is incremented by {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} on each main oscillator clock tick. Setting {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} to the main oscillator clock period in either 1 ns or 0.\+465 ns units ensures that the time stamp, read as seconds and subseconds, increments at the same rate as the main oscillator clock. For example, if the main oscillator is 25 MHz, {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} is set to 40 if digital rollover mode is selected or (40 / 0.\+465) = 86 in binary rollover mode.

In fine update mode, the subsecond increment value must be set according to the desired accuracy of the recovered IEEE 1588 clock which must be lower than the system clock rate. Fine update mode is typically used when synchronizing the local clock to the IEEE 1588 master clock. The subsecond counter is incremented by {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} counts each time a 32-\/bit accumulator register generates a carry. The accumulator register is incremented by the addend value on each main oscillator tick and this addend value is modified to allow fine control over the rate of change of the timestamp counter. The addend value is calculated using the ratio of the main oscillator clock rate and the desired IEEE 1588 clock rate and the {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} value is set to correspond to the desired IEEE 1588 clock rate. As an example, using digital rollover mode and a 25-\/MHz main oscillator clock with a desired IEEE 1588 clock accuracy of 12.\+5 MHz, we would set {\itshape ui32\+Sub\+Second\+Inc} to the 12.\+5-\/MHz clock period of 80 ns and set the initial addend value to 0x80000000 to generate a carry on every second system clock.

\mbox{\hyperlink{group__emac__api_gaf58bcf48127a67c0eda8eb96319e8690}{EMACTimestamp\+Addend\+Set()}}
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

None. 
\end{DoxyReturn}
